## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the rate law dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. Classical chemical kinetics expresses rates as power-law functions of concentration, but the inclusion of time suggests possible time-dependent forcing, reversible reactions, or complex mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of A)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions)
- Mixed order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant)
- Oscillatory forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodically driven reaction)
- Product-inhibited: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + (c2 - A)**2) (inhibition by product buildup)
- Competitive decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A) (second-order with saturation)
- Time-modulated power law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (power-law in both A and t)
- Sigmoidal rate: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple integer-order rate laws → dA_dt = c * A^n where n = 0, 1, 2, 3 are most common in elementary reactions
- Conservation of mass constraints → terms like (c - A) appear when total concentration is conserved, suggesting reversible or autocatalytic mechanisms
- Enzyme/saturation kinetics → rational functions A/(K+A) arise when intermediates are in quasi-steady state (Michaelis-Menten)
- Cooperative binding/Hill kinetics → A^n/(K^n + A^n) indicates cooperative or multi-site interactions
- Explicit time dependence in rate → suggests external forcing (light, temperature ramp) or that the ODE has been partially solved and re-expressed
- Sum of power-law terms → parallel reaction pathways each contribute additively to the total rate
- Negative terms in rate expression → indicate competing forward and reverse reactions or consumption vs production
- Rational functions with polynomial numerator and denominator in A → Langmuir-Hinshelwood surface kinetics or complex enzyme mechanisms
- Exponential dependence on t → may indicate Arrhenius-type temperature ramping where T = T0 + b*t leading to exp(c/t) or exp(c*t) terms
